                  </form> an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">سَعِدَ</foreign>, (Msb,) or of <foreign lang="ar">سُعِدَ</foreign>, (MA,) or of both: (TA:) and of <foreign lang="ar">سَعَدَ</foreign>: (K, TA:) [and also used as a simple subst.:] see <foreign lang="ar">سَعَادَةٌ</foreign> [with which it is syn.]: and see also <foreign lang="ar">سُعُودَةٌ</foreign> [with which it is likewise syn.]; <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يُمْنٌ</foreign>. (S, A.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  It is also an inf. n. used as an epithet, i. e. <hi rend="ital">Prosperous, fortunate, auspicious,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lucky,</hi> applied to a day, and to a star or an asterism [&amp;c.: so that it may be used alike as masc. and fem. and sing. and pl.: but it is also used as originally an epithet, forming its fem. with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>; and in this case it has for pl. of mult. <foreign lang="ar">سُعُودٌ</foreign> and pl. of pauc. <foreign lang="ar">أَسْعُدٌ</foreign>]: you say <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمٌ سَعْدٌ</foreign>, as well as <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ سَعْدٍ</foreign> [in which it is used as a subst.]; and <foreign lang="ar">كَوْكَبٌ سَعْدٌ</foreign>: and IJ mentions <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةٌ سَعْدَةٌ</foreign>, in which <foreign lang="ar">سَعْدَةٌ</foreign> is like <foreign lang="ar">جَعْدَةٌ</foreign> as fem. of <foreign lang="ar">جَعْدٌ</foreign>. (L.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">السَّعْدَانِ</foreign> is an appellation of <hi rend="ital">The two planets Venus and Mercury:</hi> like as [the contr.] <foreign lang="ar">النَّحْسَانِ</foreign> is applied to Saturn and Mars. (Ibn-'Abbád, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">نحس</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And [hence, also,] <foreign lang="ar">سَعْدٌ</foreign> is an appellation given to <hi rend="ital">Each of ten asterisms,</hi> (S, L, K,) <hi rend="ital">four of which are in the signs of Capricornus and Aquarius,</hi> (S, L,) <hi rend="ital">and are Mansions of the Moon:</hi> pl.       <foreign lang="ar">أَسَعْدٌ أَمْ <ref cref="n19778-1" target="سُعَيْدٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar" select="n19787"/></foreign>, meaning <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Is it a thing liked</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a thing disliked?</hi> (S, A, K,) is a prov., (S, A,) which [is said to have] originated from the fact that Saad and So'eyd, [the latter name erroneously written in some copies of the S and K <foreign lang="ar">سَعِيد</foreign>,] the two sons of Dabbeh the son of Udd, went forth (S, K, TA) to seek some camels belonging to them, (TA,) and Saad returned, but So'eyd was lost, and his name became regarded as unlucky: (S, K, TA:) Dabbeh used to say this when he saw a dark object in the night: and hence it is said in allusion to care for one's relation; and in inquiring whether a good or an evil event have happened. (TA.)                   <foreign lang="ar">حَسَكَةُ السَّعْدَانِ</foreign>, (T, S,) <hi rend="ital">to which the nipple</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">the areola</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of a woman's breast is likened:</hi> (S, K: [see <foreign lang="ar">سَعْدَانَةٌ</foreign>, below:]) the Arabs say that the camels that yield the sweetest milk are those that eat this plant: (TA:) and they fatten upon it: (Az, TA:) <hi rend="ital">it is of the kind of plants called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَحْرَار</foreign> [pl. of <foreign lang="ar">حُرٌّ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">slender, and succulent</hi> or <hi rend="ital">soft </hi> or <hi rend="ital">sweet</hi>], <hi rend="ital">dust-coloured, and sweet, and eaten by everything that is not large,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">as well as by camels,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and it is one of the most wholesome kinds of pasture:</hi> (AHn, TA:) it is <hi rend="ital">a herb,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">leguminous plant, having a round fruit with a prickly face, which, when it dries, falls upon the ground on its back, and when a person walking treads upon it, the prickles wound his foot: it is one of the best of their pastures in the days of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رِبيع</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">and sweetens the milk of the camels that feed upon it; for it is sweet as long as it continues fresh; and in this state men such it and eat it:</hi> (Az, L:) the n. un. is with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>.                   <hi rend="ital">The nipple of a woman's breast;</hi> as being likened to the [head of] prickles of the plant called <foreign lang="ar">سَعْدَان</foreign>, as mentioned above: (S, K:) or <foreign lang="ar">سَعْدَانَةُ الثَّدْىِ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">the blackness</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">areola</hi>] <hi rend="ital">around the nipple:</hi> (A:) or <hi rend="ital">the part surrounding the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ثَدْى</foreign> [here meaning <hi rend="ital">nipple</hi>], <hi rend="ital">like the whirl of a spindle.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence likewise,] <foreign lang="ar">سَعْدَانَةٌ</foreign> signifies also The <hi rend="ital">knot of the</hi>
